McNickels v. Richmond Unified School Dist.


Civ. No. 27070


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Three


11 Cal. App. 3d 1209; 90 Cal. Rptr. 562; 1970 Cal. App. LEXIS 1811



October 15, 1970 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Respondent's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied December 10, 1970. McComb, J., was of the opinion that the petition should be granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Contra Costa County, Robert J. Cooney, Judge.



DISPOSITION: We therefore conclude that respondent school district erred in failing to use the formula for deductions from salary for the absence of appellants, as set forth in Education Code section 13520. The judgment of the trial court is reversed. The matter is remanded to the trial court with directions to order compliance with Education Code section 13520 in conformity with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant teachers sought review of the judgment from the Superior Court of Contra Costa (California), which found in favor of respondent school district, finding that deductions made from appellants' salaries were proper for unauthorized absences while on strike.


OVERVIEW: Appellant teachers brought suit against respondent school district for making wrongful deductions from their salaries for unauthorized absences while on strike. Respondents had made deductions from appellants' salaries based on the number of days that school would be in session during that school year. The trial court found the deductions to be proper and the court reversed. The court held that respondent erred in failing to use the formula for making deductions from salaries for appellants' absences as set forth in Cal. Educ. Code § 13520 because the plain and unambiguous language of § 13520 included weekends and school holidays as well as actual days in the school year. The court remanded the case for a redetermination of the deductions.


OUTCOME: Judgment finding that deductions based on actual teaching days during the school year were properly made to appellant teachers' salaries for unexcused absences while on strike was reversed and remanded, because the formula prescribed by statute required that the school year include weekends and school holidays as well as the actual days the school was in session.

Scol Corp. v. City of Los Angeles


Civ. No. 35898


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


12 Cal. App. 3d 805; 91 Cal. Rptr. 67; 1970 Cal. App. LEXIS 1668



October 9, 1970 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A petition for a rehearing was denied November 5, 1970. Allport, J., was of the opinion that the petition should be granted. Appellant's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied December 3, 1970. Peters, J., and Mosk, J., were of the opinion that the petition should be granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, Robert W. Kenny, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order of dismissal is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant retailer sought review of the dismissal by the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) of its action against respondent city, for refund of tax monies paid and for declarations of constructive trusts.


OVERVIEW: Appellant retailer collected tax monies from its customers and turned them and its own monies over to respondent city. Subsequently, the tax was declared illegal and appellant sought to have the monies refunded and to have appellant and others similarly situated be declared trustees of the monies, or in the alternative, respondent be declared the trustee. Respondent requested a general demurrer against appellant and the trial court granted the demurrer without leave to amend. On appeal, the court examined the question of whether or not appellant had standing to sue, and determined that it did not, and therefore the trial court's decision was affirmed. The court found that because appellant merely acted as a tax collector, not a taxpayer, it had no standing. Further, even though appellant claimed to have paid its own monies involuntarily for the tax, the court found that all payments were voluntary and had appellant properly collected the tax from the customers, appellant would not have had to use its own monies. Finally, the court determined that, because appellant was a tax collector, not a taxpayer, appellant could not hold the position of trustee.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of appellant retailer's action, because appellant was found without standing to sue. The court determined that appellant was a tax collector, not a taxpayer, and that appellant had paid the taxes voluntarily, and therefore has no interest in the monies and no entitlement to them as a trustee or otherwise.

 

999 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Resolute Ins. Co. v. Municipal Court


Civ. Nos. 26529, 26530


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Three


11 Cal. App. 3d 1006; 90 Cal. Rptr. 337; 1970 Cal. App. LEXIS 1795



October 6, 1970 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of San Mateo County, Edmund Scott, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgments are reversed.

The matters are remanded to the superior court with instructions to enter judgments denying respondent Resolute Insurance Company's petitions for writs of review.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the Superior Court of San Mateo County (California), which reversed the grant of summary judgment in a bail bond case.


OVERVIEW: Respondent insurance company posted bail with respondent court to guarantee the appearance of a person charged with a crime, who failed to appear for his hearings. Respondent court ordered the bail forfeited, but failed to request summary judgment until the 60-day statute of limitations in effect at the time that bail was set had expired. However, within the time that appellant prosecution had to wait before requesting summary judgment, the statute of limitations was extended, and appellant requested summary judgment within the extended period. The lower court annulled the order granting summary judgment. The court found that the extension of the statute of limitations was valid because it was effected before the cause of action was barred. The extension did not impair the obligation of the contract, in violation of state and federal constitutions, because it only affected the remedy.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, as respondent did not have a vested right in the statute of limitations where it had not run in its favor, extensions were generally valid if made before the cause of action was barred, and only the remedy was altered by the change in law.

 

1000 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Anderson v. State Bd. of Chiropractic Examiners


Civ. No. 10000


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division One


11 Cal. App. 3d 963; 90 Cal. Rptr. 152; 1970 Cal. App. LEXIS 1790



October 1, 1970 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A petition for a rehearing was denied October 9, 1970, and respondents' petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied November 25, 1970.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Diego County, Hugo Fisher, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed, with directions to the trial court to enter judgment in favor of Board.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, State Board of Chiropractic Examiners, sought review of a judgment by the Superior Court of San Diego County (California) in favor of respondent chiropractors for the issuance of a peremptory writ of mandate to set aside appellant's decision to suspend respondents' chiropractic licenses for 60 days for the violations of Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 651.


OVERVIEW: Respondent chiropractors advertised a free x-ray examination to any person because of a patient's husband's donation, who was the father of a respondent, out of gratitude for his wife's speedy recovery under respondents' care. Appellant, State Board of Chiropractic Examiners, suspended respondents' licenses for 60 days for the violation of Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 651, which made it unlawful for a chiropractor to represent the price of a service at a discount, or to represent that the price for a service was less than the average price then regularly charged for the service, where there was normally not a fee charged for the services. The trial court issued a writ of mandate to reinstate respondents' licenses and the court reversed. The court found that respondents violated § 651 because respondents' represented that the services were only available to prospective patients through a donation, where the services were free to any person regardless of the donation, and, as a result, there was a representation that the free services were less than the average price. The purpose of the regulation was to prevent the bringing in of prospective patients upon a misrepresentation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that issued a writ of mandate and ruled in favor of appellant, State Board of Chiropractic Examiners, against respondent chiropractors where respondents' offer of free chiropractic services was a discount, which was less than the average price regularly charged by other chiropractors for the same services, and was, therefore, a violation of a professional rule. Respondents' licenses were suspended for 60 days.
